  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_cd6b0982-6660-4ab3-87ca-04ff45c51813'
      });
    }

              <span id="reviewTextContainer850881820" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17031515651222007674"><br/><br/>Fuck this book. Don't read it to your kids. That's the short version.<br/><br/>If you want the longer version, settle in. We're going to have a bumpy ride.<br/><br/>Also. There's spoilers here. And cussing. And some indignation. Be warned.<br/><br/>I've always thought of myself as a bit of Roald Dahl fan. I read BFG growing up and loved it. I watched Charlie and the Chocolate Factory and loved it.<br/><br/>But recently, my love dimmed a bit when I read James and the Giant Peach, a book that was a serious boatload of meh. A nickel's wo</span>
  <span id="freeText17031515651222007674" style="display:none"><br /><br />Fuck this book. Don't read it to your kids. That's the short version.<br /><br />If you want the longer version, settle in. We're going to have a bumpy ride.<br /><br />Also. There's spoilers here. And cussing. And some indignation. Be warned.<br /><br />I've always thought of myself as a bit of Roald Dahl fan. I read BFG growing up and loved it. I watched Charlie and the Chocolate Factory and loved it.<br /><br />But recently, my love dimmed a bit when I read James and the Giant Peach, a book that was a serious boatload of meh. A nickel's worth of story in a dollar-long book.<br /><br />And don't you DARE say, "Oh it's just a children's book." Or "Kids don't know any better." Or "You can't hold YA fiction to the standards of…"<br /><br />Stop. Just stop. That's such bullshit that it's an insult to the word 'bullshit.' Kid's books should be just as good as any other books. No. They should be held to a *higher* standard than other literature for the same reason that we take extra care with children's food.<br /><br />The fact is, what you feed your kids is important, and that includes what they put in their heads as well as what they put in their bellies.<br /><br />So let's talk about this book: Esio Trot.<br /><br />In this story, you have Mr. Hopper. He loves two things, the flowers he grew on his balcony, and his downstairs neighbor. Mrs. Silver.<br /><br />He's terribly lonely and he's terribly shy.<br /><br />His downstairs neighbor, Mrs. Silver, has a pet tortoise that she adores. The tortoise is named Alfie, he lives on Mrs. Silver's balcony, and Mr. Hoppy is terribly jealous of him.<br /><br />One day, Mrs. Silver laments to Mr. Hoppy. (They talk while on their balconies. She with her turtle, him tending his garden.) She's had Alfie for eleven years, and he's still tiny. She wishes he would get bigger. "I'd give *anything* to make that happen," she says.<br /><br />Mr. Hoppy gets all twitterpated hearing this, so he lies to her, telling her he knows a magic spell that will help her tortoise grow. And I quote:<br /><br />"I beg you to tell me, Mr. Hoppy. I'll be your slave for life!"<br /><br />When he heard the words <i>your slave for life</i> a shiver of excitement swept through Mr Hoppy.<br /><br />End quote.<br /><br />So he gives her some bullshit he makes up, telling her it's a spell he learned from a Bedouin. Then he goes out and buys a hundred tortoises. Then he builds a long grabber arm of the sort you would use if you wanted to, say, steal someone's tortoise off the balcony right below yours.<br /><br />At this point I thought to myself, "He's not doing what I'm thinking, is he? Then I flipped a couple pages, and told my son that it was bedtime and we'd finish the book tomorrow.<br /><br />Disappointed, he went to bed. I finished the book.<br /><br />Here's what happens: Mr. Hoppy spends the next two months slowly replacing Mrs. Silver's pet with progressively larger tortoises.<br /><br />Mrs. Silver is amazed by this, of course. And out of gratitude, she marries Mr Hoppy.<br /><br />Then Mr. Hoppy gives away all the tortoises. Including Alfie, Mrs. Silver's pet of 11 years.<br /><br />Do I really need to explain to anyone that this is fucked up?<br /><br />Do I feel bad for Mr. Hoppy? This lonely, shy man? Do I empathize with the fact that he loves someone but can't bring himself to tell her? Hell yes. I've *been* that guy. Sure.<br /><br />But his actions are fucking awful here. And their matter-of-factness makes them doubly awful. Hey there lads" it seems to say, "Love a girl? Here's what you can do! Lie to her, trick her, steal from her, make her obligated to you, then you get to be in a relationship!"<br /><br />And that's not even touching on the subject that Mrs. Silver is shown to be a complete fucking idiot, who recites a magic spell three times a day to make her tortoise grow. Then fails to notices when her beloved pet of 11 years is exchanged for a completely different animal, not just once, but several, several times….<br /><br />Suffice to say the next night when my boy asked to read the rest of the story, I deviated from the original script.<br /><br />This was made a little more difficult by the fact that the book is heavily illustrated. But even so, I was fairly confident I could do better than Dahl's original "trick her into marrying you" storyline.<br /><br />In my version, in addition to buying a bunch of tortoises and building a tortoise-grabber, Mr Hoppy also goes to the grocery store and buys a bunch of vegetables. He then spends the rest of the week inventing recipes for tortoises and testing them on his new pets, figuring out which ones are the most delicious to tortoises.<br /><br />Then, every night, he uses his long-armed tortoise grabber to lift Alfie up to his apartment where he feeds him delicious food. And, as we all know, when you eat more, you get bigger, right?<br /><br />He discovers that what Alfie likes best is some of the flowers Mr. Hoppy grows on his balcony. The flowers Mr. Hoppy loves.<br /><br />So Mr. Hoppy uses these flowers from his garden in his recipes. (I described these to my boy in some detail to pad out the story. I am a fantasy author after all.) Mr. Hoppy feeds Alfie every night, and Alfie grows bigger and bigger and bigger…<br /><br />Finally, Mrs. Silver is overcome with joy and invites Mr Hoppy down to her apartment to show off her lovely tortoise. She thanks Mr. Hoppy for his magic spell, and asks him if he'd like to have tea.<br /><br />Over tea, Mr. Hoppy says, "Mrs. Silver, I have a confession to make."<br /><br />"Yes?" she says.<br /><br />"That spell wasn't really magic," he said. "I just made it up."<br /><br />"Really?" Mrs. Silver said.<br /><br />"Yes," Mr. Hoppy said. "I've been feeding Alfie special recipes every night so he would grow bigger."<br /><br />"Oh Mr. Hoppy," Mrs. Silver said. "I already knew that. But I'm so glad you told me yourself."<br /><br />"You knew?" he said.<br /><br />"You silly man," she said. "The balcony is right outside two huge windows, just like yours is. How could I not see you grabbing him every night?"<br /><br />"Ahhh." Mr. Hoppy said, feeling rather embarrassed. He'd thought he was being pretty clever. "You're right of course. I did. You caught me. But I did it because I love you. I knew Alfie was really important to you, and I wanted you to be happy."<br /><br />"I know that too," Mrs. Silver said. "I'm so glad you're finally brave enough to tell me!"<br /><br />Then they get married.<br /><br />I would have preferred for them to go out to coffee and have a date instead, but there was a picture of them getting married in the book, so I had to leave that part in.<br /><br />In my version, they also worked together to publish a book of recipes for tortoises, and used that money to start a tortoise park, where Mr. Hoppy put his 100 now surplus-to-requirements pets.<br /><br />But apparently I was pushing my luck there. When I told him the last part, Oot gave me a look. "Did you make that up?" he asked.<br /><br />"Ahh," I said. "You're right of course. I did. You caught me. But I did it because I love you."</span>
  <a data-text-id="17031515651222007674" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <b>The Fundamental Three Facts</b>
</u><br />1) Mr. Hoppy is in love with his neighbor, Mrs. Silver.<br />2) Mrs. Silver adores her pet tortoise, Alfie, but worries about how small he is. <br />3) Mr. Hoppy gives Mrs. Silver a "magic" spell. Alfie lived with Mrs. Silver for eleven years but as soon as Mr. Hoppy swaps him out, <b>Mrs. Silver couldn't tell the difference.</b> Does friendship mean nothing? Thank goodness Dahl includes a bit at the end where we find out that <b> Alfie lived a very happy life </b> with a little girl who loved him. <div id="review_1926956770" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1926956770" />
    <a title="Matt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5903843-matt"><img alt="Matt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603562140p2/5903843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1926956770?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt" href="/user/show/5903843-matt">Matt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Matt by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/22371819-mariah-roze">Mariah Roze</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5903843-matt?shelf=children-s">children-s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5903843-matt?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1926956770" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5386165985575316613">A delightful story by Dahl I have never read, but heard much about over the past few months. Magically penned and thoroughly interesting for readers of all ages. Mr. Hoppy has long had his eye on his neighbour, Mrs. Silver. While it is an innocent admiration, Mr. Hoppy soon learns that Mrs. Silver's only love is directed towards her tortoise, Alfie. This tortoise seems to possess a weight-related issue that Mrs. Silver has said plagues her. Might solving it be the way into her heart? After conco</span>
  <span id="freeText5386165985575316613" style="display:none">A delightful story by Dahl I have never read, but heard much about over the past few months. Magically penned and thoroughly interesting for readers of all ages. Mr. Hoppy has long had his eye on his neighbour, Mrs. Silver. While it is an innocent admiration, Mr. Hoppy soon learns that Mrs. Silver's only love is directed towards her tortoise, Alfie. This tortoise seems to possess a weight-related issue that Mrs. Silver has said plagues her. Might solving it be the way into her heart? After concocting a plan than involves a magical spell and daily recitations, Mr. Hoppy takes matters into his own hands and has Mrs. Silver follow his direction. Alfie seems to grow on a daily basis and Mrs. Silver is ecstatic at the change. However, Mr. Hoppy must be careful not to tip his hand, or he may lose Mrs. Silver forever. A great story that keeps the young reader wondering until the very last page. Perfect for anyone who needs a short repose and quick entertainment.<br /><br />Dahl has mastered yet another short piece for his young readers. Steering away from the completely silly, the story holds a strong possibility of truth, though one can never know what ideas Dahl uses for his writing. Two central characters pull the readers in from the outset and the story progresses nicely from there, if only to take a few twists that keep things interesting. Basing some of the animal characteristics on pets owned by the Dahl children, the author finds a way to connect his own family to this well-developed piece. One can only hope that there are other stories out there that have just as much humour and excitement, perfect for readers of all ages.<br /><br />Kudos, Mr. Dahl for pulling me out of my 'shell' and taking the time to read this. I have loved most everything you have penned, which seems to be biographical in some way.<br /><br />Like/hate the review? An ever-growing collection of others appears at: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://pecheyponderings.wordpress.com/">http://pecheyponderings.wordpress.com/</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5386165985575316613" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/18136710" />
    <a title="sarafem" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/162057-sarafem"><img alt="sarafem" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1185759358p2/162057.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/18136710?book_show_action=true">Mar 19, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="sarafem" class="user" itemprop="url" name="sarafem" href="/user/show/162057-sarafem">sarafem</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">animal abusers, compulsive liars, and other immoral people who would enjoy a quick read.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/162057-sarafem?shelf=2008">2008</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/162057-sarafem?shelf=royally-sucked">royally-sucked</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/162057-sarafem?shelf=juvenile-7-to-10">juvenile-7-to-10</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<div id="review_2382206553" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2382206553" />
    <a title="Jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/202724-jessica"><img alt="Jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601676054p2/202724.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica" href="/user/show/202724-jessica">Jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141322797" href="/book/show/2752481-esio-trot">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/202724-jessica?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/202724-jessica?shelf=boy-s-books">boy-s-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2382206553" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13596964161340613298">I find this story of middle-aged love delightful. It's also the first chapter book that my oldest, now 13, read all the way through. He read it aloud to me when he was in kindergarten, and we both adored it.<br/><br/>Reread 2018: Since the first time I read this (or had it read to me) I've seen a ton of reviews bashing it and how sexist it is. I really don't think so. First we have to consider that it's old, second we have to consider the ending. Mr. Hoppy is over the moon that Mrs. Silver says she will b</span>
  <span id="freeText13596964161340613298" style="display:none">I find this story of middle-aged love delightful. It's also the first chapter book that my oldest, now 13, read all the way through. He read it aloud to me when he was in kindergarten, and we both adored it.<br /><br />Reread 2018: Since the first time I read this (or had it read to me) I've seen a ton of reviews bashing it and how sexist it is. I really don't think so. First we have to consider that it's old, second we have to consider the ending. Mr. Hoppy is over the moon that Mrs. Silver says she will be his "slave for life!" if he can help her get her tortoise to grow. But he's in love with her, and she with him, actually. He doesn't make her his "slave," they get married and are happy. I also saw several comments about the "poor tortoises." Which is weird. It explains exactly what happens to all the tortoises involved, and they lead very happy lives. It's a cute story. Don't overthink it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13596964161340613298" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1769128181" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1769128181" />
    <a title="James" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41609617-james"><img alt="James" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539156508p2/41609617.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1769128181?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="James" class="user" itemprop="url" name="James" href="/user/show/41609617-james">James</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141311333" href="/book/show/930032.Esio_Trot">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1769128181" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1046102262346426926">There is such a simple, straightforward and very (grown up) human story at the heart of 'Esio Trot' and it does feel somehow different from many other Dahl books in it's nature. The characters here are the key and are so well written. The humour in 'Esio Trot' is of a very gentle and affectionate kind.<br/><br/>This is a short book and a great story told by a master. To call it a 'feel-good' novel would somehow belittle and stereotype this lovely book, but there is definitely something very heart-warming </span>
  <span id="freeText1046102262346426926" style="display:none">There is such a simple, straightforward and very (grown up) human story at the heart of 'Esio Trot' and it does feel somehow different from many other Dahl books in it's nature. The characters here are the key and are so well written. The humour in 'Esio Trot' is of a very gentle and affectionate kind.<br /><br />This is a short book and a great story told by a master. To call it a 'feel-good' novel would somehow belittle and stereotype this lovely book, but there is definitely something very heart-warming here about people, life and the human spirit. </span>

He even comes up with magic words which the title is part of tortoise spelled backwards that he gives Mrs. Silver to help the turtle grow bigger. The story feels a little deceitful and it's also simply fun and I find myself enjoying the silly antics of Mr. Hoppy. It's a short little read with of Roald Dahl's wit and imagination. <span id="freeTextContainer13468255010896507551">Okay, so I read this as a sort of long distance buddy read with my seven year old niece. We’ve both got a boxset of Roald Dahl books. Mainly because she fell in love with mine while we read a couple of them together when she came to visit last year, so her mum got her a set too. She absolutely loves books and reading.   <span id="freeText13468255010896507551" style="display:none">Okay, so I read this as a sort of long distance buddy read with my seven year old niece. We’ve both got a boxset of Roald Dahl books. Mainly because she fell in love with mine while we read a couple of them together when she came to visit last year, so her mum got her a set too. She absolutely loves books and reading. Anyway, we decided to start our long distance buddy read with <i>Esio Trot</i>. We both read the book in our own homes, then as soon as we finished it, Daisy rung me to discuss the book.<br /><br />Her favourite part was the ending. I won’t go into details, as it might spoil the story. As for me, I loved Mr Hoppy and his swapping of tortoises. It entertained my mischievous side. We both had fun with the back-to-front words too. Overall, this is a fun feel-good story that we both enjoyed. I’ve been instructed by Daisy to give this 5 stars. Our plan is to read The Magic Finger next.<br /></span>

  <span id="freeText14135892618134903488" style="display:none">I'm really a huge fan of Roald Dahl's so I want to read as many of his stories as I can, while at the same time I'm dreading running out of stories to read. *lol*<br><br>This shorter story (shorter when compared to my favourites) is a cute little story about loneliness; about elderly people still wanting love and having a life; about ingenuity. Specifically, we have Mr. Hoppy, who lives in an apartment above Mrs. Silver, with whom he is in love. But he's also shy and doesn't know how to approach her - until her pet, the tortoise Alfie, gives him the perfect chance.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1489319823i/22204905._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The problem I had with this was that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Mr. Hoppy tricked Mrs. Silver and supposedly never told her the truth <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. It was all innocent and sweet and funny, but it still left me cringing a bit. <br><br>What I liked, considering the animals and pet shops portrayed in this story, was that the author included a foreword where he explained to the children (or adults) reading his book what pet shops were like then and now and why policy had to change. <br>Moreover, the author showed once again just how many ideas are floating around his head and how much he can do with simple tricks (like the "secret" of the magic language).<br><br>The book features the signature illustrations by Quentin Blake (mine, luckily, in black-and-white, not coloured like the example above).<br><br>Oh, did you know that this was made into a movie? Apparently it was, starring Judi Dench and Dustin Hoffman!</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

<span id="freeTextContainer6667576864635852532">I read this one as a child and loved it so this summer when I was looking for read aloud books for my then 5 year old this one made my short list. I <b>Loved</b> Roald Dahl books as a child and couldn't wait to start reading them to my son. This one is significantly shorter than the other books I wanted to tackle with him so I thought this would be a good place to start. <br/><br/>I figured we would start it and see how far we got before he got too fidgety to pay attention but we ended up reading it in one sitti</span>
  <span id="freeText6667576864635852532" style="display:none">I read this one as a child and loved it so this summer when I was looking for read aloud books for my then 5 year old this one made my short list. I <b>Loved</b> Roald Dahl books as a child and couldn't wait to start reading them to my son. This one is significantly shorter than the other books I wanted to tackle with him so I thought this would be a good place to start. <br /><br />I figured we would start it and see how far we got before he got too fidgety to pay attention but we ended up reading it in one sitting. He was really into it the entire time I was reading but didn't have much to say, for the most part he just listened. <br /><br />After we finished reading it I asked him what he thought.<br /><i>"Mom, I can't believe she married him after he lied to her."</i><br /><br />I was floored. Not only did that never occur to me when I read it as a kid, but i didn't even pick up on that as an issue as we were reading it aloud this time around. <br /><br />I don't care what anybody says, raising kids is hard, but raising kids that are kind and considerate is infinitely harder. In that single moment I felt like maybe I'm not totally screwing my kid up.</span>

          </span>

    <a title="Karla" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2846441-karla"><img alt="Karla" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537371209p2/2846441.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9780141801353" href="/book/show/1954055.Esio_Trot">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer257382660" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2859303080769499372">Some reviews for this book bring up interesting issues (women are dumb, animals are objects), but it just goes to show that people read the same things differently.<br/><br/>When I was done with this I felt the bigger point was that Mr. Hoppy went through so much trouble to impress Miss Silver with his magical turtle whispering and then, when he finally declares his love, she asks what kept him so long. I thought that was the message (Keep It Simple, Stupid), not that being a liar and a callous user of tu</span>
  <span id="freeText2859303080769499372" style="display:none">Some reviews for this book bring up interesting issues (women are dumb, animals are objects), but it just goes to show that people read the same things differently.<br /><br />When I was done with this I felt the bigger point was that Mr. Hoppy went through so much trouble to impress Miss Silver with his magical turtle whispering and then, when he finally declares his love, she asks what kept him so long. I thought that was the message (Keep It Simple, Stupid), not that being a liar and a callous user of turtles was the way to get a chick.<br /><br />Anyway, I liked the final pro-animal author's note from Dahl about the sad and deathly cost of the pet shop turtle trade that had, thankfully, become a thing of the past at the time of his writing.</span>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2770556069" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13938844730099898633">While I did enjoy this story for the most part, I can’t help but notice how problematic parts of it are now that I’m older. I remember reading it when I was younger and I adored it but I definitely didn’t have a full grasp of it like I did reading it again as an adult. Reading it now it kind of just gives me an unpleasant feeling, and I really don’t think it’s something I’d read to my kids. It just gives the wrong sort of message in so many ways!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

This was the shortest book on my “unread” shelf (even though yes, I read it as a child - I’m still counting it as previously unread) and I decided to start the year off promptly after midnight r</span>
  <span id="freeText12544317342551031547" style="display:none">I read this as a child, and reading it as an adult definitely reveals some other ideas... such as the ridiculousness of Mr Hoppy and how inappropriate what he does is, as well said by Patrick Rothfuss in a review of his.         <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2196889954" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16541286196208295396">Bloody 'ell! I dunno what happened here. Roald Dahl, one of the most imaginative children's writers ever has lost the plot here. He had an idea of a story and it feels like he couldn't figure how to get the story out of his head. Esio Trot is very brief, it shows you how to manipulate a daft woman and it ends very flat.<br/><br/>My daughter and I found it dull and was glad when it was over and we could move onto something else. <br/><br/>If you are a Roald Dahl fan then avoid this one because you'll only be disappo</span>
  <span id="freeText16541286196208295396" style="display:none">Bloody 'ell! I dunno what happened here. Roald Dahl, one of the most imaginative children's writers ever has lost the plot here. He had an idea of a story and it feels like he couldn't figure how to get the story out of his head. Esio Trot is very brief, it shows you how to manipulate a daft woman and it ends very flat.<br /><br />My daughter and I found it dull and was glad when it was over and we could move onto something else. <br /><br />If you are a Roald Dahl fan then avoid this one because you'll only be disappointed.</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Zgg6LJ+ZBfazTe2PK7Rk92FZuwbWecLzOdxL3imoybC9R4c+tE1mQQl6zUSIyn1BK9Z8h4QrR3/r/m5PO6xJ5Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('vRz1M6jbpxz9m+T1mwS339xCfKAb5vpsMwHqibjTwtVmU0ghgw/Eq0esxD44eq5pls27IUm0f+DhI88YqtdCgA==')})
  }
//]]>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/4273.Roald_Dahl">About Roald Dahl</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer16081518564614858033">Roald Dahl was a British novelist, short story writer and screenwriter of Norwegian descent, who rose to prominence in the 1940's with works for both children and adults, and became one of the world's bestselling authors.<br/><br/>Dahl's first published work, inspired by a meeting with C. S. Forester, was <i>Shot Down Over Libya</i>. Today the story is published as <i>A Piece of Cake</i>. The story, about his wartime adv</span>
  <span id="freeText16081518564614858033" style="display:none">Roald Dahl was a British novelist, short story writer and screenwriter of Norwegian descent, who rose to prominence in the 1940's with works for both children and adults, and became one of the world's bestselling authors.<br /><br />Dahl's first published work, inspired by a meeting with C. S. Forester, was <i>Shot Down Over Libya</i>. Today the story is published as <i>A Piece of Cake</i>. The story, about his wartime adventures, was bought by the Saturday Evening Post for $900, and propelled him into a career as a writer. Its title was inspired by a highly inaccurate and sensationalized article about the crash that blinded him, which claimed he had been shot down instead of simply having to land because of low fuel.<br /><br />His first children's book was <i>The Gremlins</i>, about mischievous little creatures that were part of RAF folklore. The book was commissioned by Walt Disney for a film that was never made, and published in 1943. Dahl went on to create some of the best-loved children's stories of the 20th century, such as <i>Charlie and the Chocolate Factory</i>, <i>Matilda</i> and <i>James and the Giant Peach</i>.<br /><br />He also had a successful parallel career as the writer of macabre adult short stories, usually with a dark sense of humour and a surprise ending. Many were originally written for American magazines such as <i>Ladies Home Journal</i>, <i>Harper's</i>, <i>Playboy</i> and <i>The New Yorker</i>, then subsequently collected by Dahl into anthologies, gaining world-wide acclaim. Dahl wrote more than 60 short stories and they have appeared in numerous collections, some only being published in book form after his death. His stories also brought him three Edgar Awards: in 1954, for the collection <i>Someone Like You</i>; in 1959, for the story "The Landlady"; and in 1980, for the episode of <i>Tales of the Unexpected</i> based on "Skin".</span>
  <a data-text-id="16081518564614858033" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
